				<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading pagetitle page-header">
					La damnation de Faust, H 111 (Berlioz, Hector)				</h1>	

				<div class="body"><div lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="wp_header">
<table>
<table>

<tr>
<th><span class="mh555">Movements/Sections</span><span class="ms555">Mov'ts/Sec's</span>
</th>
<td>4 parts
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Composition Year
</th>
<td>1845–46
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Genre Categories<span class="addpagetag mh555"></span>
</th>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="General_Information">General Information</span></h2>

<th class="wi_head">Work Title
</th>
<td class="wi_head" style="width:100%">La damnation de Faust, Légende dramatique (Opéra de concert)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th class="wi_head">Alt<span class="mh555">ernative</span><span class="ms555">.</span> Title
</th>
<td class="wi_head">The damnation of Faust, dramatic legend (Concert opera)

</td></tr>

<dl><dt><ul><li>Première partie (Plaines de Hongrie)

</dt><dd>Scène 1. Introduction
</dd><dd>2. Ronde des Paysans
</dd><dd>3. Marche Hongroise
</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><ul><li>Deuxième partie (Nord de l’Allemagne)
</li></ul>
</dt><dd>4. Faust seul dans son cabinet de travail. Chant de la Fête de Pâques
</dd><dd>5. Faust. Méphistophélès
<dl><dd>(La Cave d’Auerbach à Leipzig)
</dd></dl>
</dd><dd>6. Chœur de Buveurs. Chanson de Brander. 
<dl><dd>Fugue sur le thème de la Chanson de Brander. Chanson de Méphistophélès
</dd><dd>(Bosquets et prairies du bord de l’Elbe)
</dd></dl>
</dd><dd>7. Air de Méphistophélès. Chœur de Gnomes et de Sylphes. Ballet des Sylphes
</dd><dd>8. Chœur de Soldats. Chanson d’Étudiants
</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><ul><li>Troisième partie (Dans la chambre de Marguerite)
</li></ul>
</dt><dd>9. Tambours et Trompettes sonnant la retraite. Air de Faust
</dd><dd>10. Faust. Méphistophélès
</dd><dd>11. Marguerite. Le Roi de Thulé
</dd><dd>12. Evocation. Menuet des Follets. Sérénade de Méphistophélès avec Chœur de Follets
</dd><dd>13. Duo
</dd><dd>14. Trio et Chœur
</dd></dl>
<dl><dt><ul><li>Quatrième partie
</li></ul>

</dd><dd>16. Invocation à la nature
</dd><dd>17. Récitatif et Chasse

</dd><dd>19. Pandæmonium

</th>
<td>120 minutes
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th><span class="mh555">Composer Time Period</span><span class="ms555">Comp. Period</span>

<td><a href="/wiki/Category:Romantic_style" title="Category:Romantic style">Romantic</a>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Instrumentation
</th>
<td>voices, mixed chorus and orchestra <div class="expandline" style="background-color:#E8E8E8;margin-left:0;margin-top:0;padding:0">
<dl><dd><i>Cast</i>
<dl><dd>Marguerite (mezzo-soprano)<br />Faust (tenor)<br />Méphistophélès (baritone or bass)<br />Brander (bass)
</dd></dl>
</dd><dd><i>Chorus</i>
<dl><dd>6-part mixed chorus (SSTTBB), Children’s Chorus (SS)
</dd></dl>
</dd><dd><i>Orchestra</i>
<dl><dd>3 flutes (also 3 piccolos), 2 oboes (2nd also English horn), 
<dl><dd>2 clarinets, bass clarinet, 4 bassoons
</dd></dl>
</dd><dd>4 horns, 2 trumpets, 2 cornets, 3 trombones, ophicleide, tuba<br />timpani, percussion*, 2 harps, strings (15-15-10-10-9 players)<br />*<small>(snare drum, bass drum &amp; cymbal, suspended cymbal, triangle, tamtam, tubular bell)</small> </div>
</dd></dl>
</dd></dl>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>External Links
</th>
<td><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/La_damnation_de_Faust" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:La damnation de Faust">Wikipedia article</a><br /><span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hberlioz.com/Libretti/Damnation.htm">Libretto (Berlioz Website)</a></span><br /><span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hberlioz.com/Scores/sdamnation.htm">Online scores (Scorch format) of 3 orchestral pieces at Berlioz website</a></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Extra Information
</th>
<td>This work, which Berlioz originally subtitled as an “Opéra de concert” and later described as a “dramatic legend”, incorporates music from two prior compositions, the withdrawn <i><a href="/wiki/8_sc%C3%A8nes_de_Faust,_H_33_(Berlioz,_Hector)" title="8 scènes de Faust, H 33 (Berlioz, Hector)">8 scènes de Faust, H 33</a></i> of 1829 (H 33), and Berlioz’s arrangement of the Hungarian <i>Marche de Rákóczy</i> (H 109). The first operatic performance of the work was by the Opéra de Monte-Carlo on 18 February 1893, and the work is to the current day occasionally staged as an opera rather than in the concert hall.
</td></tr></table>
</div>
<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Misc._Comments">Misc. Comments</span></h2>
<table class="collapsible" width="90%" align="center" style="font-size: 90%">

<tr>
<th colspan="2" align="center" style="background-color:rgb(190,250,135)">Compositions and Literary Works by <a href="/wiki/Category:Berlioz,_Hector" title="Category:Berlioz, Hector">Hector Berlioz</a>
</th></tr>
<tr>
<th width="20%" style="background-color:rgb(220,250,180)">Operas
</th>
<td width="80%" style="background-color:rgb(240,250,210)">
